<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Interactions_with_humans">Interactions with humans</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Anopheles_albimanus_mosquito.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Anopheles_albimanus_mosquito.jpg/250px-Anopheles_albimanus_mosquito.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Anopheles_albimanus_mosquito.jpg/500px-Anopheles_albimanus_mosquito.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2466" data-file-height="1629" /></a><figcaption><i><a href="/wiki/Anopheles_albimanus" title="Anopheles albimanus">Anopheles albimanus</a></i> feeding on a human arm. As mosquitoes are the only vectors of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, controlling them reduces its incidence.</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Vectors_of_disease">Vectors of disease</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mosquito-borne_disease" title="Mosquito-borne disease">Mosquito-borne disease</a></div>
<p>Mosquitoes are <a href="/wiki/Vector_(epidemiology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vector (epidemiology)">vectors</a> for many disease-causing <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a> including <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoan</a> parasites. Nearly 700 million people acquire a <a href="/wiki/Mosquito-borne_illness" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosquito-borne illness">mosquito-borne illness</a> each year, resulting in over one million deaths.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EBMED2014&#95;107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED2014-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Common mosquito-borne viral diseases include <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WHO2&#95;014&#95;109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2_014-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chikungunya" title="Chikungunya">chikungunya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">dengue fever</a>, all transmitted mostly by <i><a href="/wiki/Aedes_aegypti" title="Aedes aegypti">Aedes aegypti</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WHO&#95;2009&#95;110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_2009-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-BBC250814&#95;111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC250814-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Parasitic diseases transmitted by mosquitoes include <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_filariasis" title="Lymphatic filariasis">lymphatic filariasis</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Plasmodium" title="Plasmodium">Plasmodium</a></i> parasites that cause malaria are carried by female <i><a href="/wiki/Anopheles" title="Anopheles">Anopheles</a></i> mosquitoes. Lymphatic filariasis, the main cause of <a href="/wiki/Elephantiasis_tropica" class="mw-redirect" title="Elephantiasis tropica">elephantiasis</a>, is spread by a wide variety of mosquitoes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A bacterial disease spread by <i>Culex</i> and <i>Culiseta</i> mosquitoes is <a href="/wiki/Tularemia" title="Tularemia">tularemia</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid21776596&#95;113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21776596-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Control">Control</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_control" title="Mosquito control">Mosquito control</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosquito_Netting.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Mosquito_Netting.jpg/250px-Mosquito_Netting.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Mosquito_Netting.jpg/500px-Mosquito_Netting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Mosquito nets can prevent people being bitten while they sleep.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Many measures have been tried for <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_control" title="Mosquito control">mosquito control</a>, including the elimination of breeding places, exclusion via <a href="/wiki/Window_screen" title="Window screen">window screens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_net" title="Mosquito net">mosquito nets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biological_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Biological control">biological control</a> with parasites such as fungi<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and nematodes,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or predators such as fish,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Jianguo-Dashu-1995&#95;118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jianguo-Dashu-1995-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Copepods" class="mw-redirect" title="Copepods">copepods</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dragonfly" title="Dragonfly">dragonfly</a> nymphs and adults, and some species of lizard and <a href="/wiki/Gecko" title="Gecko">gecko</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another approach is to <a href="/wiki/Sterile_insect_technique" title="Sterile insect technique">introduce large numbers of sterile males</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-twsE44&#95;122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twsE44-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Genetic modification methods including cytoplasmic incompatibility, chromosomal translocations, sex distortion and gene replacement, solutions seen as inexpensive and not subject to vector resistance, have been explored.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Control of disease-carrying mosquitoes using <a href="/wiki/Gene_drive" title="Gene drive">gene drives</a> has been proposed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Repellents">Repellents</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Insect_repellent" title="Insect repellent">Insect repellent</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Insect_repellents_in_Finnish_store.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Insect_repellents_in_Finnish_store.jpg/250px-Insect_repellents_in_Finnish_store.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Insect_repellents_in_Finnish_store.jpg/500px-Insect_repellents_in_Finnish_store.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4128" data-file-height="2415" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Insect_repellent" title="Insect repellent">Mosquito repellents</a> (including a <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_coil" title="Mosquito coil">mosquito coil</a>) in a <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finnish</a> store</figcaption></figure>
<p>Insect repellents are applied on skin and give short-term protection against mosquito bites. The chemical <a href="/wiki/DEET" title="DEET">DEET</a> repels some mosquitoes and other insects.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">CDC</a>-recommended repellents are <a href="/wiki/Picaridin" title="Picaridin">picaridin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus_oil" title="Eucalyptus oil">eucalyptus oil</a> (<a href="/wiki/P-Menthane-3,8-diol" title="P-Menthane-3,8-diol">PMD</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Ethyl_butylacetylaminopropionate" title="Ethyl butylacetylaminopropionate">ethyl butylacetylaminopropionate</a> (IR3535).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pyrethrum" title="Pyrethrum">Pyrethrum</a> (from <i><a href="/wiki/Chrysanthemum" title="Chrysanthemum">Chrysanthemum</a></i> species, particularly <i>C. cinerariifolium</i> and <i>C. coccineum</i>) is an effective plant-based repellent.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_insect_repellent" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic insect repellent">Electronic insect repellent</a> devices that produce <a href="/wiki/Ultrasound" title="Ultrasound">ultrasounds</a> intended to keep away insects (and mosquitoes) are marketed. No <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a> or university study has shown that these devices prevent humans from being bitten by a mosquito.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bites">Bites</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_bite_allergies" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosquito bite allergies">Mosquito bite allergies</a></div>
<p>Mosquito bites lead to a variety of skin reactions and more seriously to <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_bite_allergies" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosquito bite allergies">mosquito bite allergies</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sawada&#95;Inoue&#95;Kawa&#95;2017&#95;130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sawada_Inoue_Kawa_2017-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Such <a href="/wiki/Hypersensitivity" title="Hypersensitivity">hypersensitivity</a> to mosquito bites is an excessive reaction to mosquito saliva proteins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid24364549&#95;131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid24364549-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Numerous species of mosquito can trigger such reactions, including <i><a href="/wiki/Aedes_aegypti" title="Aedes aegypti">Aedes aegypti</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aedes_vexans" title="Aedes vexans">A. vexans</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aedes_albopictus" title="Aedes albopictus">A. albopictus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Anopheles_sinensis" title="Anopheles sinensis">Anopheles sinensis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Culex_pipiens" title="Culex pipiens">Culex pipiens</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Tatsuno&#95;Fujiyama&#95;Matsuoka&#95;Shimauchi&#95;2016&#95;132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tatsuno_Fujiyama_Matsuoka_Shimauchi_2016-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Aedes_communis" title="Aedes communis">Aedes communis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Anopheles_stephensi" title="Anopheles stephensi">Anopheles stephensi</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Peng&#95;Simons&#95;2007&#95;133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peng_Simons_2007-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Culex_quinquefasciatus" title="Culex quinquefasciatus">C. quinquefasciatus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Culex_tritaeniorhynchus" title="Culex tritaeniorhynchus">C. tritaeniorhynchus</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid17169531&#95;134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17169531-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ochlerotatus_triseriatus" class="mw-redirect" title="Ochlerotatus triseriatus">Ochlerotatus triseriatus</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid23352522&#95;135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid23352522-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cross-reactivity between salivary proteins of different mosquitoes implies that allergic responses may be caused by virtually any mosquito species.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pmid23442453&#95;136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid23442453-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Treatment can be with <a href="/wiki/Antipruritic" title="Antipruritic">anti-itch</a> medications, including some taken orally, such as <a href="/wiki/Diphenhydramine" title="Diphenhydramine">diphenhydramine</a>, or applied to the skin like <a href="/wiki/Antihistamine" title="Antihistamine">antihistamines</a> or <a href="/wiki/Corticosteroids" class="mw-redirect" title="Corticosteroids">corticosteroids</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrocortisone" title="Hydrocortisone">hydrocortisone</a>. <a href="/wiki/Aqueous_ammonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Aqueous ammonia">Aqueous ammonia</a> (3.6%) also provides relief.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ammonium&#95;137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ammonium-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both topical heat<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and cold may be useful as treatments.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="In_human_culture">In human culture</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Greek_mythology">Greek mythology</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Rackham-gnat_and_bull.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Rackham-gnat_and_bull.jpg/250px-Rackham-gnat_and_bull.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b8/Rackham-gnat_and_bull.jpg 2x" data-file-width="269" data-file-height="244" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Rackham" title="Arthur Rackham">Arthur Rackham</a>'s illustration of the <a href="/wiki/Fable" title="Fable">fable</a> of "<a href="/wiki/The_Gnat_and_the_Bull" class="mw-redirect" title="The Gnat and the Bull">The Bull and the Mosquito</a>", 1912</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> beast fables including "The Elephant and the Mosquito" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Gnat_and_the_Bull" class="mw-redirect" title="The Gnat and the Bull">The Bull and the Mosquito</a>", with the general moral that the large beast does not even notice the small one, derive ultimately from <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Adrados1999&#95;140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adrados1999-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Origin_myths">Origin myths</h3></div>
<p>The peoples of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> have <a href="/wiki/Origin_myth" title="Origin myth">origin myths</a> surrounding the mosquito. One <a href="/wiki/Ostiak" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostiak">Ostiak</a> myth tells of a man-eating giant, <i>Punegusse</i>, who is killed by a hero but will not stay dead. The hero eventually burns the giant, but the ashes of the fire become mosquitoes that continue to plague mankind. Other myths from the <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Yakuts</a>, Goldes (<a href="/wiki/Nanai_people" title="Nanai people">Nanai people</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Samoyedic_peoples" title="Samoyedic peoples">Samoyed</a> have the insect arising from the ashes or fragments of some giant creature or demon. Similar tales found in Native North American myth, with the mosquito arising from the ashes of a man-eater, suggest a common origin. The <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Altai_Mountains" title="Altai Mountains">Altai</a> had a variant of the same myth, involving the fragments of the dead giant, <i>Andalma-Muus</i>, becoming mosquitoes and other insects.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Lafcadio_Hearn" title="Lafcadio Hearn">Lafcadio Hearn</a> tells that in Japan, mosquitoes are seen as reincarnations of the dead, condemned by the errors of their former lives to the condition of <i>Jiki-ketsu-gaki</i>, or "blood-drinking <a href="/wiki/Hungry_ghost#In_Japan" title="Hungry ghost">pretas</a>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Modern_era">Modern era</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Winsor_McCay_%281912%29_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm/250px-seek%3D36-Winsor_McCay_%281912%29_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" data-mw-tmh="" class="mw-file-element" width="250" height="167" data-durationhint="375" data-mwtitle="Winsor_McCay_(1912)_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Winsor_McCay_(1912)_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/9c/Winsor_McCay_%281912%29_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm/Winsor_McCay_%281912%29_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="480p.vp9.webm" data-width="720" data-height="480" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/Winsor_McCay_%281912%29_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8&quot;" data-width="720" data-height="480" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/9c/Winsor_McCay_%281912%29_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm/Winsor_McCay_%281912%29_How_a_Mosquito_Operates.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="360" data-height="240" /></video></span><figcaption><i>How a Mosquito Operates</i> (1912)</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Winsor_McCay" title="Winsor McCay">Winsor McCay</a>'s 1912 film <i><a href="/wiki/How_a_Mosquito_Operates" title="How a Mosquito Operates">How a Mosquito Operates</a></i> was one of the earliest works of animation. It has been described as far ahead of its time in technical quality.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It depicts a giant mosquito tormenting a sleeping man.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Twelve ships of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> have borne the name <a href="/wiki/HMS_Mosquito" title="HMS Mosquito">HMS <i>Mosquito</i></a> or the archaic form of the name, HMS <i>Musquito</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Mosquito" title="De Havilland Mosquito">de Havilland Mosquito</a> was a high-speed aircraft manufactured between 1940 and 1950, and used in many roles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>
The Russian city of <a href="/wiki/Berezniki" title="Berezniki">Berezniki</a> annually celebrates its mosquitoes from the 17th of July to the 20th in a "most delicious girl" competition. In the competition, women stand for 20 minutes in their shorts and undershorts (British: vests), and the one who receives the most bites wins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="References">References</h2></div>
